Bethesda's lore references in Fallout games hint at future storylines, as seen with Fallout 4's Institute. Players discover hidden details in Fallout 3 even 16 years after release, sparking curiosity about future Fallout game hints.\n\nA Fallout 3 player online has noticed an interesting piece of foreshadowing relating directly to Fallout 76. It's cool to see that players still have some things to discover about Fallout 3, 16 years after its initial release.\n\nWhen it was released back in 2008, Fallout 3 received a ton of praise for its attention to detail. In fact, it's a praise that has been levied at plenty of Bethesda titles in the years since. The game was Bethesda's first effort into the post-apocalyptic franchise, and there are plenty of things players missed in Fallout 3 thanks to the sheer level of detail included in the game. With the game now 16 years old, it's fascinating that players are still discovering new things about Fallout 3, even if this particular detail was retroactively made relevant by the mere existence of Fallout 76.\n\nRelated\n\nFallout 4 Player Finds Strange Item After Hundreds of Hours of Playing\n\nAfter hundreds of hours of playing the game, a Fallout 4 player finds a strange hidden item, highlighting the smaller details in the open world.\n\nRedditor BoyDynamo shared their discovery online, which is found on a terminal in Fallout 3. When scouring the terminal for a list of \"DC Area Vault Listings,\" Vault 76 appears. There's even a full entry on the terminal, mentioning the goal of this Fallout Vault is to reopen to the world after 20 years, just as it does in Fallout 76. While it's almost certainly not the case that Bethesda planned the existence of the game as far back as 2008, it is cool to see that the studio pulled from existing lore when it came to deciding the Vault to be featured in Fallout 76.\n\nFallout 76 Foreshadowing Found in Fallout 3\n\nOther gamers in the thread pointed out that Fallout 3 features plenty of foreshadowing that can be seen in later games in the series. Fallout 4's Institute storyline is heavily alluded to in the quest, \"The Replicated Man,\" showing that some of these Bethesda references are thought through years in advance. The discovery of these kinds of things leads many to wonder about the kind of foreshadowing details that currently exist for Fallout 5 that are currently unknown.\n\nClose\n\nBethesda remains quiet on the future of the Fallout franchise. The studio is currently in the middle of development of The Elder Scrolls 6, which certainly doesn't seem set to release any time soon. It will be interesting to see what the solution is for Bethesda, as it certainly won't hand out the IP to a third-party developer lightly. It was recently revealed that Baldur's Gate 3 developer Larian was interested in making a Fallout game, and while it's unlikely at this point, revisiting this idea would certainly be the dream scenario for many.\n\nFallout 3\n\nFallout 3 is the third installment of the mainline series and has players stepping into the Capital Wasteland. {"uri": "8265513328", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-08-08", "time": "15:05:57", "dateTime": "2024-08-08T15:05:57Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-08-08T15:05:19Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.8705882430076599, "url": "https://www.gamereactor.eu/we-review-fallout-london-1417193/", "title": "We review Fallout: London", "body": "I love modding the Fallout games, I always have. I've written several articles about it, but sometimes there are very special modifications to Bethesda games that you just have to try. One such mod is Fallout London. I first became aware of this unique project a year ago, and now it's finally out after being delayed by Bethesda's attempts to update the original Fallout 4. I modded the GOG version of Fallout 4, but if you have a version of the game with all the additions, you can easily play Fallout London too.\n\nFirstly, let me explain what it takes to get Fallout London to work. If you have the game on Steam, you need to downgrade Fallout 4. Everything you need is on the Nexus Mods website, and if you search for Fallout London, you can easily find the tools. Once you've installed them, head back to Nexus Mods and install two mods through Nexus' Mod Manager Vortex: the Buffout 4 modification and the Long Loading Times Fix. Once these are in place, you're ready to explore Broken London with only a few bugs and imperfections.\n\nThe story in Fallout London stays true to the general narrative of the Fallout universe. In 2077, the US and China went to war and bombed each other back to the Stone Age. The problem with nuclear wars is that the rest of the world gets destroyed too, and that includes London, which has been well and truly levelled. You wake up in a large test tube, surrounded by two scientists who tell you that you are their best experiment, but the lab is quickly attacked and the two scientists die before you get answers. You free yourself from your glass prison and try to escape the creepy building. Along the way you meet a mysterious person, Mr Smythe, who clearly knows what's going on and who you are. He calls your character The Wayfarer before seemingly meeting his doom. You escape the building and are met by the devastation of London, where you quickly encounter some members of the Vagabond faction who take you to their headquarters. Here you'll be given your first missions and then you'll be set free in the ruined streets of London to do as you please.\n\nIt's fantastic, and Bethesda themselves couldn't have done better than Team Folon, who made the modification. One thing I quickly realised was that there is more history hidden around the corners of London. There are holotapes in many buildings that tell interesting stories from people who have been in the area. It's amazing and gives you a great insight into the world. I would say that it's actually better than what Bethesda itself does. The main story is wonderfully mysterious and the many quests you find around London are interesting, which is impressive for a group of fans. Hats off to Team Folon.\n\nFallout London is full of English charm and eccentricity. All the voice actors are native English and the dialects follow the area, which is great. You also encounter a lot of English culture. For example, one of the first missions is to find sixteen blue police boxes. If you're even a little bit of a Dr Who fan, you'll know what that means. In addition, the factions are super English. There's the Hooligan faction and further into London you'll meet the Beefeater faction, which has a penchant for human flesh. If you're an Anglophile, Fallout London is a treasure trove of English culture and \"stiff upper lip,\" and of course litres of tea.\n\nFallout London is built on the skeleton of Fallout 4, so much of the game's design will feel familiar if you've played the main game. However, Team Folon has made things more primitive by borrowing mechanics from Fallout 3 and Fallout New Vegas. First of all, your character is mute, so only the characters you meet speak. This helps with immersion as your character can make sounds as your imagination allows. The progression is a mix of the different Fallout games. You level up and earn perk points, which you get one per level. These perks are familiar from the other games in the series, but are balanced well and sometimes modified to be more useful. Some are stronger and some weaker than in Fallout 4, but they work great. I made a stealth Wayfarer, Binky Fuzzcoggle, because you have to have a silly English name. This specialised sneak was quite effective and really fun to play. You'll also find a whole bunch of cool new weapons, with only a small portion borrowed from Fallout 4. The modification system from Fallout 4 is back here, meaning you can upgrade your gear if you've picked up enough reusable junk. Fallout London is a Fallout game at its core, but the Folon team has really put their stamp on it and I had more fun at times than I did in Fallout 4 when I first played it years ago. It's crazy.\n\nFallout London is a huge game. The most popular parts of London are rendered in great detail and when you first encounter some of the most recognisable landmarks, it can be awe-inspiring. For example, I was walking around and suddenly found myself in front of The London Eye, which had now been turned into a housing estate with people living in the wheel and below. It was crazy to take the lift up to these buildings and look out over London, enjoying the detail and being impressed by how long it must have taken the Folon team to do just this small part of the modification. I had this experience all the time because Fallout London must have taken a huge amount of time. That's why the game is as big as Fallout 4 and Far Harbor combined. There are hundreds of hours of gameplay in Fallout London, and it's free. Ultra impressive! That's probably the biggest problem in Fallout London, because there are a lot of errors and bugs. Missions that don't quite work. Graphical glitches and the game crashes from time to time. Not so much after installing the Buffout modification, but it still happens, so remember to save. However, I would say it's no worse than Fallout 4 was when it first came out, and it's only minor annoyances in the grand scheme of things. Another thing that isn't the best either is the voice acting. It's generally fine, but you can notice that the sound changes depending on which microphone each actor has used. It can take you out of the experience sometimes.\n\nSo I can conclude by saying that if you're even a little bit of a Fallout fan, this mod is a must try. It's completely free and offers a fantastic take on what Fallout could be like outside the US Wasteland. It's an impressive project that provides hundreds of hours of Fallout entertainment, retaining Bethesda's game design but improving it almost universally. Well, enough of that - I need to go back and see if I can find the Tower of London and see if the Crown Jewels are there, and if they are, steal them.", "source": {"uri": "gamereactor.eu", "dataType": Aliens make a minor appearance in almost every Fallout game made. It's unclear if Fallout creators want fans to take alien lore seriously or as Easter eggs that impact canon.\n\nWhile Fallout fans were originally limited to a smaller pool of gamers who have enjoyed the series at some point in the franchise's history, with the introduction of the Fallout TV show, a whole new audience has an interest in the lore and story of the universe. While Fallout factions like the Brotherhood of Steel and the pseudo-remnants of the NCR debuted along with the show in April on Amazon Prime, there are several other factions and entire species within the games that have yet to be explored.\n\nAlthough Ghouls are obviously a central theme, other entities like mutants and Synths never made an appearance in its eight-episode run. That said, there's an even deeper-cut \"faction\" of creatures that have had a role in the vast majority of Fallout games that aren't talked about much -- either because of their limited impact on the game's overall story or their complex origins that could conflict with canon and create issues with the main narrative of the games.\n\nRelated\n\nEntire Fallout Timeline Explained: When Every Fallout Game Takes Place In Canon\n\nAlthough each game in the Fallout series functions as a mostly standalone story, they each have their place in the franchises' canon timeline.\n\nAliens Have Played A Role Throughout Many Fallout Games\n\nA Curious & Hard-To-Find Game Inclusion\n\nClose\n\nTo some, aliens fit in the retro-futuristic post-apocalyptic Atomic Age of the Fallout franchise, but to others, it takes focus away from the main narrative of human vs. human conflict. Aliens have appeared in some form in Fallout 1-3, New Vegas, Fallout 4, and Fallout 76. In the Fallout universe, several different types of aliens make an appearance, but the most predominant race are the Zeta aliens, which were further fleshed out in the Fallout 3 DLC and expansion, Mothership Zeta.\n\nIn Mothership Zeta , the Lone Wanderer gets abducted, and the DLC takes place on the alien ship.\n\nIn the very first Fallout, the aliens made a minor appearance during the special encounter called \"Alien Ship.\" During this encounter, the player can find a UFO covered in sand with the words \"Property of Area 51, return if found\" on it. There are also two aliens, one with an alien blaster. While this is the extent of the interaction, it was the first introduction to the space travelers to the game.\n\nRelated\n\nWait, Do Aliens Actually Exist In Fallout?\n\nThe Fallout TV show is missing one essential element from the video games, and here is how aliens could influence the show going forward.\n\nIt's Unclear What Impact Aliens Have On Fallout Lore\n\nIt Could Be Huge, Or It Could All Be A Joke\n\nAlthough the background of the Zeta aliens has been well fleshed out at this point, it's unclear how seriously the Fallout creators want fans to take the lore in earlier games, Mothership Zeta, and other tertiary published media like the Fallout 3 Official Game Guide, which goes into more detail about the extraterrestrial beings. According to those materials, the aliens have been around since the '60s and have influenced factions like the Enclave and even the Brotherhood of Steel via alien power cells and other technology.\n\nAlthough their impact can be felt in the game, direct interactions with Aliens outside of specific content are rare. While it could explain some of the technology found in the universe, it seems like a pretty wide catch-all to explain things away, and it's not certain whether it's just an Easter egg or meant to be taken seriously. Regardless, it's much more likely viewers will see Super Mutants and other more predominant Fallout creatures before aliens ever make an appearance.\n\nCreated by Tim Cain , Leonard Boyarsky\n\nFirst {"uri": "2024-08-448133817", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-08-08", "time": "13:07:56", "dateTime": "2024-08-08T13:07:56Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-08-08T13:00:14Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.843137264251709, "url": "https://www.dualshockers.com/places-that-would-be-the-perfect-setting-for-fallout-5/", "title": "Top Potential Locations For Fallout 5", "body": "Highlights\n\nFallout franchise offers diverse American locations, sparking speculation about potential settings for Fallout 5. Top contenders include Hawaii for a tropical paradise, Russia for a Soviet twist, and Colorado for a unique story continuation. International locations like China and Mexico also hold promise for expanding Fallout lore beyond American borders.\n\nThe Fallout franchise has always been unique in its oddly authentic depiction of their version of the world and its diverse locations.\n\nFrom Fallout 1, taking place on the West Coast of California, to Fallout 4's Eastern Coast setting of Boston, fans have walked wastelands across America, leading us to wonder where this franchise will end up next.\n\nWith Todd Howard already somewhat confirming Fallout 5, we've all been theorizing about the next potential location for this infamous franchise, so here are the top locations we at DualShockers believe would be the perfect setting for Fallout 5.\n\nAlthough the Fallout developers have stated their desire to stay within the United States, Fallout London's fan reception has had us wondering even more what international locations would fit the Fallout franchise, so we're including those, even if it's just a cry from fans. And while a lot of these locations sadly won't get an official release, you can check out many fan mods that showcase them.\n\nRelated\n\nFallout Writer Explains Jet Inhaler Was Inspired By Family's Asthma\n\nFallout 2's level designer Chris Avellone reveals the lore and real-life inspiration behind the game's Jet Inhaler.\n\n10 Hawaii\n\nA Tropical Fallout Getaway\n\nTake this location as our more exotic entry for this list. While Miami and New Orleans are other exotic American-based locations people consider, we feel the state of Hawaii can best serve Fallout's lore. With the current Fallout: Ashfall mod in the works, many of us have a hankering for a Fallout Hawaii vacation.\n\nThere are many intriguing places to imagine from a tropical Hawaiian Fallout title, like a preserved tropical hotel in the city of Honolulu, similar to New Vegas's Sierra Madre DLC, untouched for years, and a potential political commentary on the American commercialization of Hawaii.\n\nThis setting could also give Fallout a unique, water-centric, island feel, unlike anything we've had thus far. For these reasons, a tropical Fallout game will surely be on our minds for the future.\n\n9 Russia\n\nA Soviet Take On The Fallout Formula\n\nWith the Metro and Stalker series shining a light on how amazing nuclear/apocalyptic Soviet-Russian-themed games could be, many fans have attached this aesthetic to a potential Fallout project. Great examples are the many Fallout mods intended to shift Fallout's aesthetic closer to these Russian games.\n\nWith a Soviet-era aesthetic perfectly clashing against the bright post-WW2 era embodied by Fallout's retro-futuristic aesthetic of 2070s America, this would be a perfect project to mirror the games we've already played.\n\nSo, while a very unconventional idea, this retro-future Soviet setting in a city like Moscow could possibly be an amazing entry for a new Fallout game.\n\nRelated\n\nThe Outer Worlds 2 Has A Good Chance To Scratch That Fallout: New Vegas Itch\n\nThe Outer Worlds is quintessentially Obsidian.\n\n8 Colorado\n\nFallout, In The Rockies\n\nColorado has a lot of potential as an interesting location for a new Fallout game. It could bring players closer to the center of the United States, where we haven't been before. It could also give us a brilliant follow-up to Fallout: New Vegas fans have begged for, with continued stories of the Legion and NCR.\n\nWhile we fans hope this potential game is given to developers Obsidian, who are responsible for New Vegas, it's still a fun theory to think that New Vegas' amazing story could be continued with the NCR taking on the Legion in new territory.\n\n7 Philadelphia\n\nAnyone Want Radscorpion Cheesesteaks?\n\nAlongside Boston and Washington, it's clear how much Bethesda loves cities towards the eastern coast. So, alongside New York City, positioned later on this list, it's hard to escape the beckoning call coming from Philadelphia.\n\nWith places like the Freedom Trail in Fallout 4, or the Capital and Washington Monument in Fallout 3, exploring Independence Hall in Fallout 5 would fit in perfectly.\n\nAnd just like how Fallout 4 continues lore from Fallout 3, this would be a great opportunity for Bethesda to continue their self-contained part of this franchise, with returning characters and factions.\n\n6 Chicago\n\nA Trip To The Midwest\n\nLike the other great American cities on this list, Chicago's implementation lies largely in its deep-rooted history with the nation. Being tied to Ford's motorcar assembly plant, it would be amazing to see how this city in Illinois, largely bolstered by the post-war economy, could fit into Fallout's post-WW2 retro-future condition.\n\nBesides being an interesting American city on this list, Chicago's reputation in the Fallout universe has already been implemented with its importance for both the Brotherhood of Steel and the Enclave. This makes Chicago one of the top US cities that could definitely use the Fallout treatment.\n\nRelated\n\nMy Favorite Bethesda Game Is Still Fallout 4\n\nYou can always rely on the Minutemen.\n\n5 China\n\nLet's Finally Figure Out The Full Story\n\nChina was a key player in the 2077 Great War, which led to the nuclear condition of the world in Fallout. After WW2, China became one of the largest superpowers. With China mirrored to America in this new Cold War, it's clear they've always been integral to the Fallout lore.\n\nFor this reason, a game set in China could unfold much more of the underlying story that Fallout has been alluding to this whole time. With intrigue into what actually led to the bombs dropping, it's clear we've only been able to piece together the story from our sources in America.\n\nSo, even though developers would likely rather keep the games in America and a lot of the deeper lore hidden, a Fallout game in China has the potential to change everything.\n\n4 Seattle\n\nPotential For A Fallout Skyline with the Space Needle\n\nSeattle is a unique potential Fallout location for reasons unlike the others, as it has a huge amount of untapped lore potential. Other than simple geographic locations setting up for a storyline with the NCR, unlike many other States and Countries, there isn't too much we know about Seattle. With the Mod Fallout Cascadia in development, it's clear there is potential for this area as a setting.\n\nSo a Seattle Fallout game would have to do something we fans crave: create something almost completely new. New factions, settlements, and stories, set up around amazing geographical landmarks like the Space Needle, and the cold Pacific Ocean, make Seattle a gem of a likely Fallout location.\n\n3 Mexico\n\nA Fiesta For The Fallout Franchise\n\nOur interest in Mexico stems from similar factors to many other prospects: heavy pre-established lore and community interest. The Fallout: Nuevo M\u00e9xico mod is proof of community interest, and it's hard to shake how much influence this fantastic country has already had on the games.\n\nThere are huge connections to the NCR and New Vegas, with NCR Rangers commonly sent out to Mexico to patrol and claim land, similar to how they do in the Mojave. With a variety of potential new factions and a ton of great desert land for that traditional Fallout feel, Fallout in Mexico is one of the most exciting potential Fallout experiences.\n\nRelated\n\nCould A New Version Of Fallout New Vegas Be On The Way?\n\nThey asked me how well I understood theoretical games. I said I had a theoretical degree in games.\n\n2 New York City\n\nA Fallout Full Of Skyscrapers\n\nAs mentioned previously, Bethesda loves the north-eastern province of America. The beautiful Appalachian mountains and monuments in Washington, though, are nothing compared to the skyscraping potential of one of America's most powerful cities.\n\nWith the known presence of Mutants in New York mentioned by the Brotherhood in previous games, in New York, we'd have a lot of classic fun to look towards. Yet, it's difficult for many games to replicate New York for an important reason: the large city brings a subsequently large scope.\n\nYet, this is exactly what makes Fallout in New York so intriguing. The potential of what the developers pull from the ashes of a retro-future New York is unlimited, making New York a top contender for Fallout 5.\n\n1 Texas\n\nI Can See That Lone Star From A Thousand Miles Away\n\nFans want more Fallout in Texas, and we at DualShockers do, too. It's hard to shake the feeling that a game similar to Fallout: New Vegas would shine in the Lone Star State. With a great desert of oddities, lore, and that classic New Vegas western cowboy feel, we'd love to visit Texas in a Fallout game sometime in the future.\n\nSure, we've technically already been to Texas with the spin-off Fallout: Brotherhood of Steel, but It's about time we re-established Texas as the true arbiter of the next Fallout game. If the assumed true ending of New Vegas was the NCR victory, then it's safe to assume we'd continue their story, with or against them, toward the east.\n\nIf a Texas project is given a chance, we hope the project is given to Obsidian. Regarding Obsidian's involvement in Fallout: New Vegas, Todd Howard has stated:\n\n\"there's only one group we trust to do this... It's either this group or nobody.\"\n\nObsidian consists of amazing storytellers connected to Fallout 1,2, and New Vegas, and we can't understate how important their involvement would be.\n\nWhile Fallout 5 is far into the future, whether from Bethesda in a game on the East Coast or given to Obsidian for the continuation of New Vegas, we hope, among them, Texas is highly considered for Fallout 5, or even a future Fallout project.\n\nFallout 4\n\n9/ 10\n\nRPG\n\nAction\n\nSystems\n\nOpenCritic Reviews Top Critic Rating:87/100 Critics Recommend:89%\n\nFranchise Fallout\n\nPlatform(s) PC , PS4 , PS5 , Xbox One , Xbox Series X , Xbox Series S\n\nReleased November 10, 2015\n\nDeveloper(s) Bethesda\n\nPublisher(s) Bethesda\n\nEngine Creation\n\nESRB M FOR MATURE: BLOOD AND GORE, INTENSE VIOLENCE, STRONG LANGUAGE, USE OF DRUGS\n\nX|S Enhanced No\n\nFile Size Xbox Series 51 GB (December 2023)\n\nMetascore 87\n\nPS Plus Availability Extra & Premium\n\nSteam Deck Compatibility yes\n\nCross Save no\n\nCross-Platform Play no\n\nExpand\n\nNext\n\nEvery Fallout Game Ever Released, Ranked\n\nThey say war never changes, but Fallout certainly has changed over the years. This project offers players a chance to explore a post-apocalyptic version of London, expanding the Fallout universe beyond its usual American settings. {"uri": "8259400357", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-08-05", "time": "04:15:03", "dateTime": "2024-08-05T04:15:03Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-08-05T04:13:51Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.8274509906768799, "url": "https://screenrant.com/fallout-show-voice-actors-characters-return-original-roles/", "title": "13 Actors From The Fallout Games Who Could Easily Play Their Own Characters In The Show", "body": "Fallout Season 2's Setup Could Finally Force A Major Missing Faction Out Of Hiding Summary Fallout season 1 features original characters but hints at potential cameos from beloved Fallout game actors in future seasons. Actors like Clancy Brown, Ron Perlman, and Richard Dean Anderson could potentially reprise their roles in the Fallout TV adaptation. Fans eagerly anticipate possible appearances from famous actors such as Brad Garrett, Liam Neeson, and Danny Trejo in Fallout season 2.\n\nWith the success of Fallout season 1 owing largely to its memorable ensemble, gamers-turned-viewers are already speculating about which actors from the Fallout games could play their own characters in the show. Although the retrofuturistic world of Fallout remains the same throughout its many franchise entries, each game in the series takes place during different stages of Fallout's post-apocalyptic timeline and in various locations throughout the former United States. Set 219 years after the bombs drop, Amazon Prime Video's Fallout unfolds after all the franchise's preexisting games, making it perfect for cameo appearances.\n\nFor the most part, Fallout's cast of characters in season 1 were original personalities created for the show, from the ever-determined Vault Dweller Lucy (Ella Purnell) to the ruthless bounty hunter The Ghoul (Walton Goggins) to Brotherhood of Steel initiate Maximus (Aaron Moten). In Fallout season 1's ending, the show indicates that its sophomore outing will take place in New Vegas -- the setting for one of the most beloved games in the series. As a result, some of the Fallout series' most famous cameos could make the leap to the TV adaptation too.\n\n13 Clancy Brown Rhombus\n\nA prolific voice performer and live-action actor, Clancy Brown has appeared in everything from SpongeBob SquarePants to Shawshank Redemption. Set to star in Max's upcoming The Batman spinoff, The Penguin, Brown has also lent his talents to cult classics like HBO's Carnivale. In Fallout, Brown voices Brotherhood of Steel knight Rhombus, the Lost Hills chapter's head paladin. Stoic and gruff, Rhombus could easily be portrayed by Clancy Brown in the live-action series too, especially if the sophomore outing delves deeper into the Brotherhood of Steel's vision for the Wasteland.\n\nRelated Fallout Season 1 Review: Prime Video's Stellar Adaptation Leans Into The Offbeat & The Brutal\n\nPrime Video's long-awaited Fallout TV series adaptation knows its viewers well -- and it isn't afraid to give them a Vault Boy-style wink.\n\n12 Ron Perlman The Narrator / Butch Harris\n\nMost well known by Fallout fans for being the voice of the series' disembodied narrator, it's kind of shocking that Ron Perlman's voice didn't make it into the Amazon Prime Video adaptation, even if Perlman's most iconic Fallout quote did. The Hellboy actor voiced the opening and closing narrations for Fallout, Fallout 2, Fallout 3, Fallout: New Vegas, Fallout 76 and Fallout Tactics, though he also lent his talents to portraying onscreen characters, including Fallout's Butch Harris and a newscaster in Fallout 4. While the Fallout TV show is packed with Easter eggs, a Ron Perlman cameo is a must.\n\n11 Richard Dean Anderson Killian Darkwater\n\nThe mayor of Junktown in 2161, Fallout's Killian Darkwater also runs the community's general store and heads up their defensive forces. As the player character comes to learn during the game's side quests, Killian has a strong sense of \"frontier justice,\" making him a pretty compelling Wastelander. He's also voiced by a pretty compelling actor: Richard Dean Anderson, who's most well-known for playing the original MacGyver. Given the Fallout series' love of all things retro, and its on-point references to Hollywood and the entertainment industry, Anderson would be a fun get.\n\nRelated 11 Biggest Changes Amazon's Fallout Show Makes To The Video Games\n\nThe Fallout show serves as the newest canon entry to the franchise, but it also went back to change several elements of the established lore.\n\n10 Brad Garrett Harry\n\nComedian and actor Brad Garrett is pretty synonymous with the Ray Romano-led sitcom Everybody Loves Raymond, though he's also lent his singular voice to animated projects like Finding Nemo and Ratatouille. While the post-apocalyptic Fallout may seem like a stretch for Garrett, his comedy chops could easily work for the show's dark humor and offbeat sensibility. Better yet, he's voiced Fallout's Harry, a super mutant stationed in the watershed in Necropolis. Although he's mentioned again in Fallout 2, Harry has yet to reappear in the series, but he'd be a great addition to the TV show's ensemble.\n\n9 Liam Neeson James\n\nThe Taken actor might be associated with his action roles and Star Wars appearances, but he also memorably voices the protagonist's father in Fallout 3.\n\nRelated Exciting Fallout Season 2 Update Makes Me Much More Confident About The Video Game Show's Future\n\nAfter Fallout's exceptional first season, I'm even more confident about its future after the Prime Video show's latest production update.\n\n1 8 Cree Summer Tandi\n\nA prolific voice actor, Cree Summer has actually voiced several characters in the Fallout universe.\n\n7 Danny Trejo Raul Tejada\n\nActor Danny Trejo crops up in plenty of action film fare, from Machete and Heat to Predators and Once Upon a Time in Mexico. However, he also has an incredibly memorable role in the Fallout series.\n\nRelated I'm So Glad Amazon Put My Biggest Fallout Season 2 Fear To Rest\n\nWhen it comes to the Emmy-nominated Fallout TV adaptation, our greatest fears about the sophomore outing have been addressed -- and it's great news.\n\n1 6 Malcolm McDowell John Henry Eden\n\nThe star of Stanley Kubrick's A Clockwork Orange, Malcolm McDowell has also appeared in Star Trek: Generations and the Halloween movie series. In Fallout 3, the actor voices John Henry Eden, an advanced ZAX AI unit installed in a military complex northwest of Washington, D.C.\n\n5 James Urbaniak Doctor 0\n\nWhile James Urbaniak has starred in searing comedies like Difficult People, the actor also appears in dramatic film and TV projects, from Christopher Nolan's Oscar-winning Oppenheimer to The Fabelmans. In the world of Fallout: New Vegas, Urbaniak voices Doctor 0, a pre-War scientist and member of the Think Tank operating in Big MT.\n\nRelated Fallout Continues A Positive Awards Trend After The Last Of Us Made Emmy History\n\nLast awards season, The Last of Us made Emmys history as an incredibly decorated video game adaptation, and, this year, Fallout continues the trend.\n\n1 4 Lynda Carter Magnolia\n\nThe original Wonder Woman, Lynda Carter voices Fallout 4's Magnolia, a singer who performs at a neighborhood bar called the Third Rail. A musician in her own right, Carter also recorded the songs \"Good Neighbor\" and \"Train Train\" for Fallout 4.\n\n3 Ashly Burch Tina De Luca, Rowdy Or Cricket\n\nOne of the stars of Apple TV+'s Mythic Quest, Ashly Burch is perhaps even more well known for her video game voice work. In addition to lending her talents to Fallout, the Emmy-winning Burch has voiced Aloy in Horizon Zero Dawn and Horizon Forbidden West, Chloe Price in the Life Is Strange series, Mel in The Last of Us Part II, and Tiny Tina in the Borderlands series.\n\nRelated Fallout Season 2's Setup Could Finally Force A Major Missing Faction Out Of Hiding\n\nA major faction currently missing from Fallout's TV show could be forced to reveal themselves after what happened in the season 1 finale.\n\n2 Ahmed Best Carver Timmerman\n\nIn 1999, Ahmed Best provided the voice and motion-capture performance for Star Wars: Episode I -- The Phantom Menace's love-him-or-hate-him character, Jar Jar Binks. More recently, the prolific voice actor made a triumphant return to the Star Wars universe by portraying Jedi Kelleran Beq in The Mandalorian.\n\n1 Wayne Newton Mr. New Vegas\n\nOne of the most popular singers in the US during the 20th century, Wayne Newton has performed in Las Vegas, Nevada since the early '60s -- a feat that earned him the moniker \"Mr. Las Vegas.\" In a funny homage to Newton's success, the singer voices Mr. New Vegas in Fallout: New Vegas, an AI personality who serves as the city's DJ.\n\nFallout season 1 is streaming on Amazon Prime Video.\n\nFallout 4.0 Drama Where to WatchSeasonAllSeason 1 streamrentbuy\n\nNot available\n\nNot available\n\nNot available\n\nstreamrentbuy\n\nNot available\n\nNot available\n\nNot available\n\n*Availability in US\n\nBased on the video game franchise of the same name, Fallout is a drama series set in post-apocalyptic Los Angeles. Fortunately, all is not lost, as players can fix these crashes by following these simple steps:\n\nDownload the Buffout 4 mod from Nexus mods and place it in the Fallout 4 folder. Do not download any additional files when prompted. Look for the F4SE folder in the Buffout 4 zip file and copy it. Locate the F4SE folder in the Fallout 4 folder and replace it with the one from the Buffout 4 zip file. Now, locate the f4se_loader.exe file and launch the mod. Use this executable file every time you need to launch the mod. To make it easily accessible, create a shortcut on your desktop. When you want to start the mod, right-click on f4se_loader.exe and select Run as administrator. If you do not want to do this every time, access the compatibility settings in the Properties menu and tick always run as administrator.\n\nAfter following the steps mentioned above, you will not run into major crashes, especially after the train cutscene. Improve enemy AI with mods like the Commonwealth Encounter Pack and the Immersive Fallout Combat Mod. Balance gameplay by testing the new slide against challenging foes like Deadlier Deathclaws.\n\nGiven the amount of combat the average Fallout 4 player will see in a campaign, it just makes sense to install this mod which improves movement by making everything much smoother and more action-orientated. One of the most widely held beliefs regarding the fourth mainline game in the Fallout franchise is that while its role-playing elements feel underbaked, its combat is leagues ahead of every other installment. Having said that, it's still fairly clunky, especially when so many modern shooters have figured out how to handle movement through a first-person perspective.\n\nThanks to bp42s over on Nexus Mods, the \"Enhanced Movement\" mod adds a wealth of new features to Fallout 4 that make the game more fun to control. Many of the adjustments are minor but have a major impact on movement; Sprinting while outside of combat no longer drains AP while directional movement speed has been reduced by 25% when backpedaling and 15% when strafing. Yet the biggest addition is the ability to slide, which boasts a unique animation and allows the Sole Survivor to use their weapon in the middle of the action.\n\nRelated\n\n10 Fallout 4 Mods That Make The Game Feel Like The Fallout TV Show\n\nWhether it's realistic character models or environmental adjustments, these mods make Fallout 4 feel more like Prime Video's TV series.\n\nHow To Improve Fallout 4's Combat\n\nA Little Modding Never Hurt Anyone\n\nWhile it's true that Fallout 4's combat is much better than the likes of Fallout 3 and New Vegas, it could be better. Beyond the clunky movement, enemies aren't especially difficult to defeat given that the AI running them isn't too smart, meaning they either stand in one place waiting to be shot or simply charge ahead with little self-preservation. There are ways to fix this as the modding community has had just under a decade to refine Bethesda's original combat mechanics.\n\nOne of the best mods Fallout 4 players can download to spice up combat is the Commonwealth Encounter Pack, which introduces an extra 290 random encounters to the vanilla game. Many of these can be tricky to overcome, making exploration and progression a more meaningful process. To improve enemy AI, the aptly named Immersive Fallout Combat Mod is exactly what's required as it makes foes more intelligent, enabling them to better flank and outmaneuver the Sole Survivor.\n\nThose Fallout 4 players wanting to put their new slide to the test can even do so against suped-up versions of the game's most challenging enemies thanks to the Deadlier Deathclaws mod. Having more realistic movements will likely already make the game much tougher, so it might be the case that installing more difficult mods could be a bridge too far. Finding the balance in battle is essential to enjoying the Commonwealth Wasteland.\n\nSource: bp42s/Nexus Mods\n\nFallout 4\n\nRPG\n\nAction\n\nFranchise Fallout\n\nPlatform(s) PC , PS4 , PS5 , Xbox {"uri": "2024-08-443886206", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-08-04", "time": "21:27:49", "dateTime": "2024-08-04T21:27:49Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-08-04T21:00:11Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7490196228027344, "url": "https://screenrant.com/fallout-london-best-things-first-early/", "title": "Fallout: London - Best Things To Do First", "body": "Upon starting your adventure in the new Fallout 4 mod, Fallout: London, it can be overwhelming to know what to do first in a foreign and unfamiliar land compared to the traditional Fallout franchise. With your pockets empty and the lack of weapons and ammo in your possession, setting out can be as dangerous as it is thrilling.\n\nFortunately, there are a few things you can do to help you survive and thrive in London's wasteland. By prioritizing a few personal objectives, from finding useful weapons and allies to searching for a safe haven, you will be set up and ready to face the city's unchartered waters.\n\nRelated\n\n10 Biggest Fallout: London Changes & Differences\n\nFallout: London is a total conversion mod that has changed almost everything in Fallout 4 to give players the closest thing they can get to a sequel.\n\nFind A Weapon\n\nMelee Weapons Are More Common\n\nUnlike Fallout 4, where you're given a gun right off the bat, Fallout: London doesn't offer such liberties, and players must acquire one themselves while exploring. Moreover, melee weapons are far more abundant than firearms and ranged options, so you may have to rely upon these until you find your weapon of choice. There are some firearms you can still get early on in the game:\n\nScoped Hair Trigger Crude Gun\n\nTo obtain this weapon in Fallout: London, players must head northeast until reaching the River Thames, following the path to the Train Crash. You will know you're going in the right direction when you see a Layton Towers sign. From here, turn right and follow the road for a short distance.\n\nHead through the gap in the broken wired fencing to your left, going towards the edge of the river bank, where you'll see a large copper-colored pipe. Jump over the railing to enter the pipe, where you'll find a duffle bag and ammo container beside it. You can pick up x4 .32 Rounds, x11 9mm Rounds, and the Scoped Hair Trigger Crude Gun inside.\n\nFlare Gun\n\nAvailable to obtain within the first main quest in Fallout: London is the Flare Gun. The quest will lead you to encounter the Thamesfolk in Thameshaven, their underground hideout. Head northwest past the Fesco (inspired by the real UK supermarket, Tesco) to meet some guards, who suggest you take the southern entrance into a tube station.\n\nEnter and make your way through the flooded and radioactive tunnels until you find some chain alarms and a tin-can trap. On the right side, you will see a room containing a cooking station and a bed, showcasing that someone lived here. The Flare Gun is on the bedside table, along with a bunch of Flares for ammo.\n\nWhile it's not the best gun, with a slow fire rate, it will serve its purpose, considering that the alternative is to use your bare hands. Hold on to these until you find better options or vendors to purchase weapons from.\n\nCollect Tickets\n\nFallout: London's In-game Currency\n\nRather than Bottle Caps in Fallout 4, the primary trading currency in Fallout: London is Tickets, which are used to travel around London's Underground system. You will have picked up a few of these upon first escaping the lab through the station barriers and entering London Bridge Station within the tutorial.\n\nThese valuable orange tokens are abundantly scattered around the city wasteland and should be collected whenever spotted. Doing so will allow you to explore and get around London on the tube network and barter for items and useful gear with vendors.\n\nRelated\n\nHow To Adopt Churchill The Bulldog In Fallout London\n\nFallout: London features an adorable new companion in the form of Churchill the bulldog, who can be adopted early on into the mod's story.\n\nRecruit Companions\n\nSeven Companion Characters\n\nAs companions are a large part of the Fallout franchise, many players will want to recruit followers in Fallout: London, either for some good company or help in combat. Many of these NPCs offer engaging side quests in Fallout: London and storylines, so it is worthwhile searching for a few early on in the game. At the start, you can readily recruit three out of seven companions before progressing the main quest or joining factions to meet the rest.\n\nChurchill, The British Dogmeat\n\nFans of Fallout 4 will most likely be looking for their ever-loyal German Shepherd companion, Dogmeat, or another equivalent canine companion. Luckily, Fallout: London provides its version of the furry friend, Churchill, a British Bulldog. You can recruit Churchill early on as your first companion after escaping the lab.\n\nUpon surviving the train crash, you'll be met by a group of ruffians named the Vagabonds in Fallout: London, led by Sebastian Gaunt. Speak to them, and they will tell you about the Thamesfolk settlement, pointing you in its direction.\n\nHead north until you find Prilladog Food Factory, where you'll hear a guard yelling for some dogs to stop fighting. When you arrive at the scene, you'll see a bulldog, Churchill, fighting a group of mongrel dogs. To save Churchill, slaughter all the mongrels and speak to the guard, who will let you keep him as your pet.\n\nAside from being able to follow players or stay put, Churchill can do some nifty tricks at your command and even search the surrounding area for useful items. Overall, he is a great companion to take along with you on your apocalyptic adventure.\n\nArthur Mountbatten\n\nArthur Mountbatten is a friendly ghoul companion in Fallout: London who you can recruit early on while exploring the London wasteland, as long as you cross to the north side of the River Thames. To find him, travel to the northeast corner of the map, heading towards Hackney Way, where you will find a large gate.\n\nFrom here, head directly north from the Tower of London side of Tower Bridge. Then, make your way to the large concrete wall marked with the 'Hackney Checkpoint' glowing sign.\n\nBe careful as you approach, as you will see a group of hooligans along the wall to your right, which you must kill before going any further.\n\nArthur can be found strung upside down from a tree to the left of the wall. If you speak to him, he will ask the player to help him get down, triggering a dialogue option for you to free him. Upon doing so, you can invite Mountbatten to travel with you, but make sure your party isn't full if you want the ghoul in Fallout: London as your follower.\n\nMad Jack\n\nSimilarly to Arthur Mountbatten, Mad Jack is an accessible companion early on if you explore the north side of the River Thames, specifically near Trafalgar Square. Mad Jack is an extremely strong companion, befitting of a bodyguard who will keep you safe as a tank-based sidekick in post-apocalyptic London.\n\nYou can find him inside the basement of a pub called Pilgrim heading northwest from Trafalgar Square, going towards the bend facing Regent's Park. The pub is located along one of the side streets, around two roads away from the map's boundary.\n\nHead inside the pub and go towards the backdoor to find the lounge area leading into the underground Fight Club. You must speak to the fight manager to get Mad Jack's attention, which will put you in a fight against him, and you must survive for over a minute.\n\nThe only way to unlock Mad Jack as a companion character is to allow the fight between you to take place. Make sure you don't initiate combat until after the promoter makes the announcement, which will cause Jack to become temporarily hostile. To wrap up the quest, you don't have to beat him, but you must survive the fight, so reload the save if you face your demise.\n\nBuild Settlements\n\nUnlock Two Early Settlements\n\nAs with settlements in Fallout 4, those in Fallout: London make great trading hubs and safe player bases to call home among the terrors that await in the foreign apocalyptic wasteland. Setting these up around the map will allow you to create your own houses, recruit settlers, and store your valuable items and gear, which are important priorities to consider when starting the game.\n\nWhile each settlement provides unique benefits and advantages, along with useful allies, a few stand-out settlements are worth unlocking at the start of Fallout: London and are available almost immediately after the tutorial.\n\nLondon Bridge Settlement\n\nPlayers will be familiar with London Bridge, which is the first area they will reach after the tutorial. It is one of the best settlements in the game, as it is central to most points of interest around the map and has two access points. Moreover, it comes with Beefy, an ex-Beefeater, and six other settlers, who are running the toll bridge scam when you first meet them.\n\nWhile the settlement is easy to reach, you are required to pass a challenging Charisma (6) and Intelligence (5) Check, along with 10 Tickets to cross the bridge. If you speak to Beefy and pass these checks, he will request that you assassinate his former boss and clear the Beefeaters in the area. Accepting and succeeding in this side quest in Fallout: London will reward you with the London Bridge settlement.\n\nBiggin Hill Airport\n\nThe next best settlement to go to at the start of the game is Biggin Hill Airport, which is also available right after the tutorial, though it may take a little longer to acquire. carlosreyes11 on YouTube says to go directly west from Churchill Library and speak to the Tree Man named Gordo, the yoga teacher.\n\nIf you offer your help to the settlement, he will send you north to an underground bunker to take care of some hostile Dryads. Hack the terminal to get inside and take out the turrets along with the Dryads before facing a formidable Legendary Glowing One inside. Upon clearing these enemies, speak to the Synapse Tree and then report back to Gordo, who will tell you to return to him in a few days.\n\nTo avoid waiting to speak to Gordo again, you can find a bed and wait for two days, resetting your world time in the Fallout 4 mod . Upon returning to Gordo, he will grant you access to the Biggin Hill Airport Workstation and settlement, and you will be named Head Druid.\n\nSource: carlosreyes11/YouTube\n\nFallout Many Fallout games have replicated that feeling of leaving the vault in the years following, but the first still holds a special place in many hearts. Fallout Vault 13 is a brand new Fallout 4 mod that aims to recreate that moment - and the entire first game - and it's got a demo you'll be able to play surprisingly soon.\n\nFirst announced in 2021, Fallout Vault 13 is an ambitious mod for Fallout 4 which doesn't just plan to plonk the first game in the newer RPG, but to remake it entirely. A couple of years ago the modding team working on the project announced a demo but since then there's been a few periods of radio silence, with some assuming the project would never see the light of day. It encompasses Vault 13, Vault 15, and the budding settlement of Shady Sands - Fallout TV show watchers will no doubt remember that name. As this is a Fallout 4 mod, the team has had to build an entire wasteland to surround these areas complete with additional caverns and places to explore, some of which you can see in the Shady Sands Showcase released in 2022.\n\nPresumably there's been a lot of progress since then but even that earlier version of the village is familiar to anyone who's played the original Fallout. Seth, Aradesh, and Razlo are all present but Tandi is conspicuously absent, though admittedly this may be due to another quest from the original game. You can also grab a few glimpses of Vault 13 and Vault 15 here, as well as everyone's favorite radscorpion caves.\n\nFor me, I can't wait until the mod includes Junktown. Dealing with Gizmo has always been a favorite quest of mine, with multiple ways to complete it showcasing the flexibility and range of approaches possible in this apocalyptic title. The Master rendered with modern gaming graphics also promises to be a treat, as even in the 1997 original's art style he managed to become one of the creepiest villains in gaming.\n\nThe Fallout Vault 13 demo will be playable from Thursday August 8 from 6pm PDT / 9pm EDT / Friday August 9 from 2am BST / 3am CEST. Team FOLON is working on a hotfix to address crashes and glitches, along with a future patch. Players experiencing issues with the mod can receive one-on-one tech support from the developers.\n\nFallout 4's expansive Fallout: London mod is one of the most impressive community-driven add-ons in recent memory, but developer Team FOLON wants players to know that it's working to improve the state of the game. Shortly after its launch, which was a long time coming after several substantial delays, Fallout: London stunned everyone with its attention to detail, writing, and dedication to delivering a familiar but unique experience. Unfortunately, the current version of the mod is riddled with bugs, a problem of which Team FOLON is very aware.\n\nPer PC Gamer, Team FOLON announced on its Discord that it's currently developing a hotfix that should alleviate many of the more pressing issues plaguing players. The main intention of the hotfix is to mend any problems causing severe crashes and game-breaking glitches while also adding a pre-existing mod to the package called \"Buffout 4.\" Said add-on has long been used to stabilize Fallout 4's engine, fixing several major bugs and adding a crash logger so Team FOLON is at least able to track certain breakages and prioritize removing them from Fallout London.\n\nRelated\n\nFallout: London Proves That One Mainline Fallout Trend Needs To Change\n\nFallout: London introduces a host of new content to players, and one inclusion is a reminder of the lack of diversity in one mainline feature.\n\nFallout: London Has A Bright Future\n\nTeam FOLON Is Working With The Community\n\nAside from the hotfix, Team FOLON also announced that it's developing what it describes as a \"HUGE\" patch that will fix prolific problems like floating objects and various quest-related bugs. There's no word yet on when this patch is expected to roll out but given the size of the team and Fallout: London's unstable nature, fans could be waiting for a while. Fortunately, the developer is offering another solution for those desperate to play the mod: One-on-one tech support.\n\nPlayers who join Team FOLON's Discord can request individual troubleshooting sessions with the developers if they're battling to access Fallout: London because of a bugged install or persistent crashes. That kind of dedication to working with the community is impressive, especially given that at the end of the day, this is a not-for-profit mod. If it wasn't already obvious, it should now be clearer than ever that Team FOLON is passionate about its creation and wants as many people to enjoy it as possible.\n\nThose players who have managed to dodge Fallout: London's rampant crashes and bugs have stated that the mod feels like a genuine piece of DLC forFallout 4. Many of the mechanics and systems are familiar to fans of the franchise but the new setting, weapons, and story make for a fresh change of pace. Since Bethesda isn't planning on setting a Fallout game anywhere other than the United States, it's fun to see a glimpse into a post-apocalyptic United Kingdom, even if it isn't canon.\n\nSource: PC {"uri": "2024-08-445925244", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-08-06", "time": "15:57:26", "dateTime": "2024-08-06T15:57:26Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-08-06T15:47:41Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7058823704719543, "url": "https://gamerant.com/fallout-4-london-how-adopt-find-recruit-churchill/", "title": "How To Recruit Churchill & Find Him After Dismissal", "body": "Quick Links\n\nWho Is Churchill In Fallout: London?\n\nHow To Find & Recruit Churchill In Fallout: London\n\nFallout 4's largest mod to date, Fallout: London, is finally here, and with it, players are able to explore what happened to other countries during The Great War (at least, fan interpretations of what happened, Bethesda is still tight-lipped about it). The mod takes place in London, England, and players get to meet all kinds of interesting NPCs,\n\nWhile playing Fallout 4, players will quickly run into Dogmeat, arguably one of the best companions in the game. Thankfully, players will run into a Dogmeat in London as well, except this one is named Churchill, and he is an English Bulldog (the best option for the companion). Here's how to find him, recruit/adopt him, and then find him after dismissing him.\n\nRelated\n\nFallout London: How to Find a Settlement Early\n\nFallout London makes finding a safe place to store all your loot and build a base harder than Fallout 4, so here's how to find an early Settlement.\n\nWho Is Churchill In Fallout: London?\n\nClose\n\nChurchill is one of the many companions players can find and recruit in Fallout: London. Named after Winston Churchill, this dog takes on the role of Dogmeat while in London. He is an adorable English Bulldog who loves the player and is more than happy to explore the world of post-Great War London with them. He is also one of the best companions in the mod, just like Dogmeat was in the base game.\n\nRelated\n\nFallout London: All Factions (& How To Join Them)\n\nFallout London offers players different Factions. Here's how to join them all.\n\nHow To Find & Recruit Churchill In Fallout: London\n\nChurchill is found at the Prilladog Food Factory, which is actually found pretty close to the starting area (just like Dogmeat is). Once there, players will find Churchill being attacked by various stray dogs and will need to rescue him. Upon rescuing him, a nearby guard will get mad at the player for killing the dogs and will ask if they want to take Churchill with them since they have no use for him. Upon saying yes, the dog will follow the player just like any other companion in the game. From then on, the dog will follow the player until being dismissed; however, after being dismissed, players have had trouble finding the dog.\n\nRelated\n\nHow to Fix Fallout London Crashes\n\nIf you're having trouble with crashes while playing Fallout London, try these fixes.\n\nHow To Find Churchill After Dismissing Him In Fallout: London\n\nIf Churchill is dismissed, one of three things can happen. He can disappear from the game entirely, which is a known bug that the developers are working on fixing currently. Another option is that he can be replaced by Dogmeat, another known bug that is being worked on (and Nexus Mods has a fix for that). However, the final option, which is also the option that is supposed to happen, is that Churchill will end up at the docks near the ferryman on the northern part of the Thames. From there, he can be recruited again like normal.\n\nIf Churchill isn't at the docks, players may need to wait for the developers to fix the known bugs that are causing him to disappear.\n\nFallout Here's how to find and recruit them!\n\nHow To Download Fallout: London On A Steam Deck\n\nClose\n\nFirst, before players can get started with this process, they will need to make sure that they have the following on their Steam Deck (and the Steam Deck must be in desktop mode):\n\nFallout 4: Game of the Year Edition (the mod requires all the game's DLCs except for the High-Resolution Texture Pack) 200 GB of free space (thankfully, players only need this during the installation process) The Heroic Games Launcher (from the Discover Store) The Fallout: London Downgrader Tool from Nexus Mods (the Linux version is required)\n\nRelated\n\nAll Settlements & Their Locations in Fallout London\n\nFallout London has 6 Settlements (7 if you count a home). Here's how to find them all.\n\nOnce players have all of this done, they can then begin the process of actually downloading the mod. To do so, follow these steps:\n\nDownload the game Put the Steam Deck into desktop mode Use the Heroic Games Launcher to sign into GOG and \"purchase\" Fallout: London (the game is free, but it will still say purchase) Go to Heroic Games Launcher's library and install the mod Download the downgrader tool and extract it from the ZIP file it is in Load the tool, log into Steam, and select the location of the game (it is automatically /home/deck/.steam/steam/steamapps/common/Fallout 4/) Select the option to downgrade the version of the game Navigate to the folder with the mod and find the installer (the automatic location should be /home/deck/Games/Heroic/Fallout London/) Right-click on the installer and select the option to add it to Steam Go to Steam and change the installer's compatibility to Proton 9.0-2 (to do this, just go to the preferences menu for it) Launch the installer using the Steam shortcut option and navigate to where the game is installed (/home/deck/.steam/steam/steamapps/common/Fallout 4/) After the installation is finished, close the installer and bring over the game's INI files To do this, go to the /home/deck/Games/Heroic/Fallout London/_Config folder and find the 3 files labeled .INI Transfer those 3 files to the /home/deck/.local/share/Steam/steamapps/compatdata/377160/pfx/drive_c/users/steamuser/My Documents/My Games/Fallout4/ folder\n\nRepeat step 12 but with the files in the AppData folder To do this, go to the /home/deck/Games/Heroic/Fallout London/_AppData folder Transfer all those files to the /home/deck/.local/share/Steam/steamapps/compatdata/377160/pfx/drive_c/users/steamuser/My Documents/My Games/Fallout4/ folder\n\nMove the Fallout4.ini file to the launcher To do this, go to the /home/deck/Games/Heroic/Fallout London/_Config folder and find the file labeled \"Fallout4.ini\" Transfer that to the /home/deck/.steam/steam/steamapps/common/Fallout 4/ folder\n\nDisable Cloud Saving {"uri": "8265597292", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-08-08", "time": "16:05:34", "dateTime": "2024-08-08T16:05:34Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-08-08T16:04:43Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.686274528503418, "url": "https://www.vg247.com/our-favourite-things-in-fallout-london", "title": "Jeremy Bentham, Doctor Who, and horse meat - our favourite things in Fallout London", "body": "Fallout: London, the DLC-sized mod -- which is a complete lie given how gargantuan this mod is -- from Team FOLON launched on July 25. Now that the team at VG247 has had enough time to wet their appetites and see what this highly-anticipated mod is all about, we decided to discuss and share a few of our favorite things across post-apocalyptic London.\n\nThe mod is, unsurprisingly, full of neat Britishisms (not that there's anything great about being British), and Easter eggs which are a real joy to experience. Sure, Fallout: London hasn't been without its fair share of bugs and crashes (which is authentic to the Bethesda experience, if you ask me), but this hasn't removed from the amazing amount of passion and detail that has gone into making Fallout: London a reality.\n\nWithout further ado, here are some of our favourite things in Fallout: London.\n\nMark Warren: \"What's a Gentry?\" my Fallout: London character, a mustachioed man built for sniping and not much else, asks the head in a jar. Jeremy Bentham, the founder of modern utilitarianism, stares back at me. His cold, dead, preserved eyes glare into my soul. WHAT did you just say, they seem to enquire. His protectron body should probably be punching me in the face with a metal limb.\n\nIt doesn't.\n\nBecause Jeremy Bentham -- or rather his preserved corpse -- is a gentleman. He believes in healthy debate, and that's exactly what he was trying to have with me before I rudely defied the laws of stupidity. He slowly realises it's not worth it. I don't have any views on The Gentry, and even if I can cobble some together once he tells me what they are, they won't be worth hearing.\n\nHe politely brings the debate to a close, and as we part he hands me a cookie. I stand on the steps leading up to University College London, trying to process what's happened in the blur that was the last five minutes, after I spotted the robot and thought 'No way, it can't be'. Eventually, I bring up my inventory and have a munch on the cookie.\n\nMy dumb character might not be sure about the whole \"the greatest happiness of the greatest number that is the measure of right and wrong\" thing that the philosopher's dead body is peddling. But I sure got a kick out of this bit of Fallout: London.\n\nJim Trinca: My favourite thing about Fallout London is a bold situational pun at the very opening: you. in a giant test tube, being examined by two doctors who are voiced by two Doctors. Specifically Colin Baker and Sylvester McCoy, the 6th and 7th titular stars of Doctor Who, most infamous for leading the show during its terminal decline in the late eighties.\n\nColin Baker's tenure was notoriously cack, and McCoy's, while a marked improvement, simply wasn't enough of a turnaround to save the show from its eventual cancellation in 1989. One of the main reasons cited for such was the unassailable quality of science fiction shows coming out of America at the time: particularly Star Trek: The Next Generation. The Brits, thought the BBC, simply cannot compete with shows that have actual money behind them.\n\nAnd there will never be an official installment of Fallout set in the UK, for it is an American story about how America sees itself. But the Brits have, somehow, knocked together something that holds up. Through endless hours of bedroom coding, the calling in of countless favours, and sheer tenacity, there is a British Fallout that's just as meaty as a real, mainline installment.\n\nAnd so I think the fact that the first NPCs you meet in this remarkable project are ex-Doctor Whos. The very ones in fact that presided over the original show's demise. It's a statement of intent: this is a proper game project with proper access to proper talent that you've actually heard of. And like all good British science fiction, we made it with two yoghurt tubs and a bit of string, and still managed to blow everyone away with its bold vision and eccentricity.\n\nAlso I haven't played past the opening.\n\nKelsey Raynor: Scrambling through post-apocalyptic London is pretty dangerous as it is. There's Hooligans, Gatherers, Beefeaters and all manner of ghastly, mutated creatures for you to be cautious of in Fallout: London. There's foxes with brutal bites, giant ladybugs that I felt awful killing, and scuttle crabs that square up to you.\n\nAn enemy I wasn't prepared for, however, was the Royal Mail. One of the few trusted mail delivery services in the UK -- that is actually reliable -- is far from reliable in Fallout: London.\n\nI walked past plenty of red post-boxes in my first few hours of the game without trouble. In fact, one of my earliest screenshots of the game is of a postbox. Nothing amazing, but I was certainly amazed to see one in Fallout for the first time. My amazement wore off when one of the things jump-scared me, however.\n\nThat's right. Some of Fallout: London's post-boxes aren't defunct relics from a time when posties' red vans were on every corner. No. Some of them have instead been turned into Post Boxers; post-boxes that'll jump out when you least expect it, conjuring wheels from beneath them and saws for hands.\n\nMy previous obsession with looting post-boxes in the hopes they'd have some money inside was quickly put to bed, and I have been avoiding post-boxes ever since. Though, there is a friendly one in Westminster to look forward to.\n\nKelsey Raynor: Sweeney Todd is a tale from the 1800s, detailing the life of a barber who'd murder his clients using his razor-sharp tools. He'd dispose of the bodies by handing them over to downstairs neighbor, Mrs. Lovett, who would then use these victims as ingredients for 'mystery meat pies'. It's quite grim, really, but so is post-apocalyptic London.\n\nIf you explore the streets surrounding St. Paul's Cathedral during the day, you can find Fleet Street, which is where Sweeney Todd resided. Take a wander down the road, and you'll actually see a barber shop led by a disheveled man called Ted. And would you look at that? His neighbor, Mrs. Miggins, happens to be a baker, and there's a corpse-shaped bin bag just outside... I wonder what they're both up to.\n\nExplore a little further, and you'll find a bucket of human remains behind Mrs. Miggins counter.\n\nThe interaction sadly doesn't consist of much more than Ted actually giving you a haircut and his baker neighbor being a trader, but it's still quite neat to see the old, gruesome tale brought to life in Fallout: London.\n\nMark Warren: Yes, all of my bits are about Protectrons designed to mirror iconic Brits. Look, I'm a New Vegas fan, robot fetishism kinda comes with the territory.\n\nAnyway, getting back on track, John Bercow's cameo in Fallout: London is a little thing, but it's a perfect example of the mod going that extra mile to deliver an experience that feels authentically English, complete with all of our bonkers traditions and bizarre sense of humour.\n\nAs you'll see if you're from another part of the world and you play the mod, we're a nation - establishment-wise at any rate - committed above all else, in a frankly psychopathic fashion, to the notion of order. Of everyone doing what they're told. At least in theory, those rules obviously often don't apply to those at the top, at least in any terms beyond appearance.\n\nSo, having a man in there literally known for shouting 'Order!' at MPs during his time as speaker is just chef's kiss. And it's quite funny too.\n\nKelsey Raynor: In case you hadn't heard, the UK and other parts of Europe were at the center of quite the scandal in 2013. A scandal involving horse meat. That's right. Folk across the country were buying 100% beef burgers and God knows what else only to later have it revealed that these food products did, in fact, have traces of horse DNA inside them. It also happened that Tesco was at the forefront of the scandal, while other stores such as Aldi and Lidl were also affected.\n\nWhile consuming horse meat isn't actually a health risk, this did cause a lot of understandable concern about how horse DNA ended up in our food. If that could happen, what else was ending up in our food that we didn't know about?\n\nAnyways, if you explore the aptly-named Fesco in Fallout: London, you can find 'Meat Mix Burgers' which have all manner of animals on the packaging. One of them, of course, is a horse, which is undeniably a gentle poke at the food-safety concerns of Brits during 2013 and the meme that the whole scandal later became.\n\nFallout: London has a lot of niche references like this, which is what makes the mod so brilliant. Take the random NPC's in Westminster that talk about napping in Parliament, for example. That actually happened. {"uri": "8263562507", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-08-07", "time": "12:48:42", "dateTime": "2024-08-07T12:48:42Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-08-07T12:47:50Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6666666865348816, "url": "https://www.inverse.com/gaming/fallout-london-review", "title": "'Fallout: London' Is The Most Surprisingly Terrifying Game In The Series", "body": "Three hours into Fallout: London, I wander through a rundown supermarket scrounging for canned goods and medicine to help me on my journey north. Things are going swimmingly.\n\nBetween checking shelves for food and medical supplies, I cut down the occasional oversized fly for some minor XP before noticing a small opening along the wall in the distance. I walk over, hoping to find a computer terminal or a freezer with even more rations to take with me. As I round the corner into the opening, what greets me instead is the absolutely enormous thorax of a creature I've never seen in my cumulative 300 hours of playing Fallout games. I backpedal as it turns towards me and behold just how badly I screwed up. This is The Bloatmother. It's five times my size and doesn't look happy about what I've been doing to her babies.\n\nI clumsily swap my switchblade for the 9mm pistol I found a few blocks away. I use the V.A.T.S. to line up three of the 17 shots I have and fire. The first two ricochet off its hardened body. The third finds flesh, but barely makes a dent in the beast's health bar. The Bloatmother fires a volley from its pinchers, but before it can hit me I hit the pause button and walk away from my Steam Deck.\n\n\"Nope.\"\n\nTense moments like these are the early highlights of Fallout: London, the ambitious unofficial Fallout 4 expansion from Team FOLON. These superb moments of terror are punctuated by the mystery that pervades this post-apocalyptic city. Players are a long way from the familiar wastelands of America, and Fallout: London reminds them of that often.\n\nI haven't had such a raw, guttural reaction to Fallout's brand of body horror since I first crossed paths with Centaurs in 2008.\n\nThe Fallout franchise has been around for 27 years. In that time, its enemies, factions, and fiction have become iconic in gaming (and now television). While the grit and grime of the Fallout universe remain effective, there is comfort in walking around an America ravished by nuclear fallout all these years later. There's nostalgia in shooting Rad Scorpions in the Mojave Wasteland to the tune of the oldies. Three-Dog's charming interstitials recounting the horrors of post-apocalypse Washington D.C. make me feel at home.\n\nThose luxuries don't exist in Fallout: London. Setting the game in the European metropolis has wiped the slate clean, allowing Team FOLON to reintroduce and reimagine the franchise, and subvert players' expectations.\n\nThere are brand-new creatures in the wild with new attack patterns, animations, and gross mannerisms. Returning enemies look slightly different and are tougher than ever. And the setting is refreshing, with London extending a new coat of paint to its factions and people.\n\nBethesda's games have always looked at how pre-apocalypse culture gets re-interpreted by those hundreds of years in the future following humanity's downfall, and Fallout: London is no different. Camelot, a gang inspired by 20th-century soldiers and The Knights of the Round Table, adds a dash of righteous camp not seen since New Vegas' charming gang of Elvis impersonators. The Gentry are the descendants of the English aristocracy, an interesting, slightly more civilized twist on the antagonistic patriarchy of Cesar's Legion. Seeing how a nuclear apocalypse and time have warped English culture is fascinating, a credit to Team FOLON's world-building.\n\nThe marriage of Fallout 4's more modern gameplay and New Vegas' exemplary role-playing mechanics is a match made in heaven.\n\nMy favorite of the new groups is the Thamesfolk. While I won't spoil their reveal here, I'll say their visage inspired a need to learn everything I can about the origins of these people and exactly how radiation changed them so irrevocably. I haven't had such a raw, guttural reaction to Fallout's brand of body horror since I first crossed paths with Centaurs in 2008.\n\nWhat brings Fallout: London's mystery full circle is its difficulty. Enemies are not messing around and can slaughter players in an instant. Radiation is an ever-present threat players must be mindful of, making meds like Rad-X and Radaway invaluable. These elements add a sense of risk-reward to discovering factions, locations, and creatures.\n\nIn other words, Fallout: London is a must-play. The marriage of Fallout 4's more modern gameplay and New Vegas' exemplary role-playing mechanics is a match made in heaven, one that occasionally surpasses Bethesda's 2015 game. However, unraveling the many mysteries tucked away in this new setting is easily the star of Team FOLON's effort. You truly never know what lurks around the corner in post-apocalyptic London.
