{"uri": "2024-08-446766083", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-08-07", "time": "10:36:15", "dateTime": "2024-08-07T10:36:15Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-08-07T10:00:11Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6627451181411743, "url": "https://gamerant.com/fallout-london-every-all-stat-explained/", "title": "Fallout: London - Every Stat, Explained", "body": "Highlights\n\nFallout: London mod offers a new gameplay experience in England, relying on Fallout 4 mechanics with a new story and map. The Strength stat in Fallout: London is crucial for melee builds, increasing damage and carrying capacity for players. Investing in Perception improves VATS accuracy, helps detect enemies, and is essential for ranged combat and spotting loot.\n\nFallout: London is a complete makeover mod for the popular role-playing game, Fallout 4. The mod was in development for five years before being released in July 2024. As the name suggests, the gameplay takes place in the City of London, England.\n\nRelated\n\nFallout 4: Children of Atom, Ranked\n\nThe Children of Atom make a major comeback in Fallout 4's Far Harbor DLC. Here are the best of them, ranked.\n\nThe Fallout: London mod relies on the mechanics of the base game, layering a new map, environment, and story on top. This means that players need to understand what each stat is, the impact they can have on gameplay, and where to put attribute points for specific builds. It is easy to make a mistake during character creation, and end up with a set of stats that simply don't work.\n\n7 Strength\n\nImportant For Melee Builds\n\nIncreases carrying capacity Increases melee damage\n\nStrength is one of the seven stats in Fallout: London. As one may imagine, the Strength stat is a measure of a character's physical ability. Investing attribute points into strength is vital for players who intend to go with a melee build.\n\nRelated\n\nFallout 4: 10 Best Unique Weapons & How To Get Them\n\nWhile unique weapons in Fallout 4 aren't easy to come by, they are also very powerful, and these unique weapons are worth the effort to track down.\n\nStrength has two primary benefits in Fallout: London. Firstly, for every point invested in Strength, the player will do an additional 10% melee damage. Secondly, for each point spent in Strength, the player can carry an additional 10 weight. Even players who do not intend to use a melee weapon might find a couple of points in Strength useful, just for the extra carrying capacity.\n\n6 Perception\n\nBe More Aware Of The Environment\n\nImpacts VATS accuracy Detect enemies more easily\n\nPerception is the main stat that Fallout: London players who want to specialize in ranged combat will want to invest in. Some builds, such as a sniper build, rely on high Perception to be able to target specific body parts when using VATS from long range.\n\nAdditionally, higher Perception makes it easier to spot lootable items and enemies in the environment. This combines well with a ranged damage build, as enemies will be spotted from much further away, and can be engaged at range before they spot the player. Another benefit of a high Perception statis that it will greatly improve the player's skill at lockpicking.\n\n5 Endurance\n\nMore Health And Stamina\n\nIncreases hit points Longer sprint duration\n\nEndurance is a stat in Fallout: London that every player needs to take a close look at. It is crucial for building a character that has at least some level of survivability. The main benefit of putting points into Endurance is that it will increase the number of hit points the player has.\n\nHowever, Endurance has a couple of other important benefits. Firstly, the more stamina a player has, the longer they will be able to sprint for. Secondly, radiation resistance is increased by spending points in Endurance, which can be very useful when exploring the open-world map.\n\n4 Charisma\n\nOften Overlooked But Useful\n\nHelps to get better prices with vendors Assist with colony management\n\nCharisma is, in general, a non-combat stat. Many players that enjoy Fallout: London as a quest-based, FPS game will likely ignore the Charisma stat completely. However, players that enjoy the RPG aspects might like to consider spending some points in Charisma.\n\nRelated\n\nFallout 4: 8 Worst Settlements\n\nFallout 4 introduced player settlements to the series, bringing new ways to interact with the world. But some locations are a mistake.\n\nWhen completing quests, high Charisma has a chance of helping get past speech checks. Charisma is also checked when issuing commands to a companion; the higher a player's Charisma, the more likely a command will be successful. Additionally, higher Charisma makes it easy to attract new dwellers to a settlement and manage them.\n\n3 Intelligence\n\nDirectly Impacts Experience Point Gains\n\nIncreases experience point payout Makes crafting and modding items more effective\n\nMost Fallout: London players will want to put at least a few points into the Intelligence stat, simply for the fact that the higher a player's Intelligence, the more experience points they gain for every applicable activity.\n\nHowever, Intelligence is also useful for players who enjoy crafting their own gear, and modding weapons and armor, as well as crafting their own consumables such as medication and explosives. Lastly, hacking is impacted by a player's Intelligence, with higher Intelligence leading to a better chance of a successful hacking.\n\n2 Agility\n\nGreat For Stealth Gameplay\n\nImproves sneak ability Adds action points for VATS\n\nFallout: London rewards players who want to rely on a stealth build by presenting plenty of opportunities to use the sneak ability tactically. Agility is the primary stat that impacts the player's sneak ability, and is therefore vital for stealth builds.\n\nRelated\n\nFallout 4: 7 Items You Should Never Sell To Merchants\n\nWhile some items are completely fine to sell for extra Caps in Fallout 4, these are ones that you should hold onto.\n\nFurthermore, the higher a player's Agility, the more action points they will have available to spend while using VATS. On top of this, the player's movement speed is driven by their Agility. Overall, Agility is a powerful stat that can have a massive impact on gameplay, especially for sniper or assassin-style builds.\n\n1 Luck\n\nWe All Need A Little Luck Now And Then\n\nIncreases crit chance Impacts loot quality\n\nThe Luck stat should not be overlooked by Fallout: London players. It has an impact on many of the core gameplay mechanics, providing either overt or hidden benefits in many scenarios. In combat, Luck directly impacts critical hit chance, and can also randomly mitigate certain negative effects.\n\nThe higher a player's Luck stat, the more chance they have of finding more loot, and better grade loot as well. This means that Luck also has an impact on crafting and modding, as the player is more likely to find the materials they need if they have high Luck.\n\nFallout {"uri": "2024-08-447847841", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-08-08", "time": "09:05:10", "dateTime": "2024-08-08T09:05:10Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-08-08T08:33:38Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6509804129600525, "url": "https://gamerant.com/fallout-london-best-early-game-weapons/", "title": "Fallout: London - Best Early Game Weapons, Ranked", "body": "Highlights\n\nFallout: London mod offers a total game transformation with unique items and open-world map. New players must scavenge for weapons in London Shard, finding Molotov and Cane early on. Progressing in the game leads to more weapons like the Balisong, flare gun, 9mm pistol, and service rifle.\n\nSome mods for Fallout 4 simply tweak the gameplay mechanics. Others add new items such as weapons and armor. But there are some mods that entirely transform the game, and Fallout: London is such a mod. This is a total makeover of the original game with its own storyline, open-world map, and unique items.\n\nRelated\n\nFallout 4: 10 Best Unique Weapons & How To Get Them\n\nWhile unique weapons in Fallout 4 aren't easy to come by, they are also very powerful, and these unique weapons are worth the effort to track down.\n\nNew players to the Fallout: London mod will notice very quickly that they are not spoon-fed an easy playing experience. They are not given a weapon, or any consumables such as blood bags or food for healing. They must progress some way before being so equipped. However, there are a few basic weapons that can be found within the first hour or two of play in this post-apocalyptic RPG.\n\n7 Molotov\n\nSave It For The Radshrews\n\nWeapon Stats: Damage: 51 Fire rate: 0 Range: 93 Accuracy: 0\n\nOnce a new player in Fallout: London has managed to leave the lab, where the new player tutorial takes place, they will find themselves in the London Shard. This is a liminal area that acts as a transitional zone between the tutorial and the game proper.\n\nRelated\n\nFallout 4: 8 Worst Settlements\n\nFallout 4 introduced player settlements to the series, bringing new ways to interact with the world. But some locations are a mistake.\n\nThere are a few useful items to be found in this zone, and one of these is a single Molotov cocktail, which is thrown like a grenade. It can be found inside the public toilets on the ground floor. This is well worth picking up, as shortly after, the player encounters a large group of roaches, and will likely have no other weapon at this stage.\n\n6 Cane\n\nSteal It From The Skeleton\n\nWeapon stats: Damage: 15 Speed: Medium\n\nOnce a Fallout: London player has worked out how to leave the London Shard, they will find themselves in London Bridge Station. Just as the player enters this area, they will spot a skeleton sitting on a bench.\n\nLeaning against the skeleton's arm, is the cane. This is a basic melee weapon, but good enough to take out the odd roach or radshrew in a pinch. It works well until the player gets the next weapon on this list, at which time it becomes superseded.\n\n5 Balisong\n\nA Cool Trick Knife\n\nWeapon stats: Damage: 14 Speed: Fast\n\nOnce a Fallout: London player has discovered a way out of London Bridge Station, they will find themselves in the Lewisham area. At the start of this zone, the player will meet a group of three NPCs, who are part of a local gang.\n\nIf the player chooses to hang with the gang, they are awarded with the Balisong, which is a cool butterfly knife that can be used as a weapon and to do tricks. It doesn't do a lot of damage, but it has a fast attack rate, and is useful in the early part of this role-playing game.\n\n4 Flare Gun\n\nMinimal Ammo But Useful\n\nWeapon stats: Damage: 9 Fire rate: 3 Range: 35 Accuracy: 74\n\nFollowing the main story arc in Fallout: London, will send the player to the Thamesfolk quite early on. This faction lives in a warren of underground tunnels, which the player can explore and loot. One location that will be discovered is an old tube station, which is where the flare gun is located.\n\nThe player needs to continue along the tunnels until they come to a series of alarms that have been set up using some old cans. This guards a place that has been inhabited at some stage, and inside is a sleeping room with a bed and a bedside table. On that table is the flare gun and a few flares to use for ammo.\n\n3 9mm Pistol\n\nDon't Miss This Weapon\n\nWeapon stats: Damage: 16 Fire rate: 66 Range: 83 Accuracy: 61\n\nThe first hour of Fallout: London will generally involve a player using their fists to fight off radshrews (much like radroaches). And with little in the way of healing consumables to loot, this can be a problem for some builds. But there is a 9mm pistol available quite early in the game, that many players might miss.\n\nRelated\n\nFallout 4: Best Items To Get in Far Harbor\n\nEvery DLC for Fallout 4 added a variety of new items for players to acquire, and here are the ones in Far Harbor that players should focus on.\n\nOnce the player has found their way down to London Bridge Station, they will need to use a ticket to open the ticket gates to the platforms. However, just before these ticket gates is a derelict shop. Inside that shop is a serving counter, and below that counter is a small safe that can be picked. Inside is a 9mm pistol and a limited amount of ammo.\n\n2 Service Rifle\n\nIt's A Smelly\n\nWeapon stats: Damage: 33 Fire rate: 4 Range: 215 Accuracy: 73\n\nThe service rifle is modeled on the Short Magazine Lee Enfield (SMLE), or as British Tommy's called it in both World Wars, the Smelly. This rifle is available very early in the game, close to the location of the 9mm pistol in London Bridge Station.\n\nTo the right of the ticket booth in the station, is the preservation center, with a locked door that can be opened by a player with enough strength. Inside is the service rifle. It doesn't do a lot of damage, but it is useful until better options are available.\n\n1 Longsword\n\nNot Quite Excalibur\n\nWeapon stats: Damage: 33 Speed: Medium\n\nMelee players who are willing to befriend the Arthurian Knights faction, can gain access to the longsword quite near the start of Fallout: London. However, not until they have completed the Thameshaven zone.\n\nRelated\n\nThe Best Fallout 4 Mods, Ranked\n\nFans of Fallout 4 have been making mods for the title ever since it was released. Here's a look at some of the absolute best of the best, ranked.\n\nOnce they have, they can locate the Swan and Mitre pub, and close by is a building with a lot of roaches. Inside this building is the usual junk loot, but also the longsword. {"uri": "8262049766", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-08-06", "time": "15:15:58", "dateTime": "2024-08-06T15:15:58Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-08-06T15:15:23Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6235294342041016, "url": "https://www.pcgamesn.com/fallout-76/legendary-crafting-interview", "title": "Fallout 76 is making one massive change, and it's pulling me back in", "body": "The Fallout 76 Milepost Zero update makes bold changes to legendary crafting, reducing reliance on luck in the wasteland survival game.\n\nIf you've played a lot of Fallout 76, there's a good chance you've reached a point where improving your build can feel almost beyond your reach. With the upcoming Milepost Zero update, which is currently in public testing, Bethesda is cracking open its crafting system in a bold new fashion. Ahead of its full release, PCGamesN sat down with lead producer Bill LaCoste and creative director Jon Rush to discuss the change and what it means for the future of the revitalized multiplayer RPG.\n\nThe Fallout 76 Milepost Zero update is making some smart improvements to the six-year old Bethesda survival game. It's changed a lot in that time, from that notorious, much-maligned launch to the modern day, where it's become what might be the most fun way to spend time in the Fallout universe. Now, Milepost Zero is taking the next step, with new features that are the perfect way to fill downtime between events and daily ops.\n\nAnother key change that will likely cause even more dramatic shake-ups is the new legendary crafting system. Put simply, this is a much more open-ended way to approach putting Fallout 76's most powerful, build-defining mods onto items. Previously, getting your hands on the best legendary mods to create the ultimate gear has been a largely random process, requiring you to gamble valuable resources to craft an item and hoping that you hit the specific effect you want on it.\n\nThat's all changing in Milepost Zero. Now, every time you scrap a legendary item there's a small chance that you'll learn the ability to craft one of the legendary mods it bears, in much the same way that you unlock crafting for standard mods. Once you've picked up the skills to make a specific legendary mod, you'll be able to build modules for it at the Tinker Bench using legendary particles (earned from the scrapping process), and then either apply them to weapons and armor, or sell them through your camp shop to other players.\n\n\"Really the crux of the decision was to rely less on an exclusively RNG experience to get that gear that you want,\" Rush tells me. \"Our players have specific playstyles they want to adhere to, and they want the gear to be able to support that. So what this does is it gives players agency - rather like a little tiny light at the end of the tunnel. So you can at least see what you're progressing towards; where you want to go.\"\n\n\"What's also kind of cool is it also sort of opens up a whole new economy in the game,\" Rush continues. \"So, okay, I scrapped something and - oh - now I know how to create Bloodied mods. Well, I'm rich now!\" For those out of the loop, 'Bloodied' refers to a particularly popular legendary modifier that amplifies your damage when your character's health is low, and is core to many players' favorite builds - including mine. As such, the idea of being one of the first players to learn the ability to make and sell ready-to-cook Bloodied mods to others is rather enticing.\n\nI'm certainly convinced by the proposal. As someone who's poured hundreds of hours into Fallout 76, I reached a point where I had an almost perfect loadout for the build I wanted. Unfortunately, that meant that unless I completely swapped it out for something different (which would itself necessitate many more hours of starting from scratch), the chance of getting any upgrades on my gear was so slim that it didn't feel worth pursuing further.\n\nWith this new legendary crafting system coming into action in Milepost Zero, those upgrades feel like they might feasibly be attainable. Plus, as I also discussed with Rush and LaCoste, the new Fallout 76 caravan routes are a great way to make sure you aren't just left sitting around waiting for some action. Perhaps it's time to strap on the power armor once again and get to work.\n\nIf that's not enough to keep you busy, check out our Fallout London review to see if the ambitious fan-created project is worth your time. We've also got more of the best games like Fallout to try if you can't wait until we finally get a Fallout 5 release date.", "source": {"uri": "pcgamesn.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "PCGamesN"}, {"uri": "2024-08-447391749", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-08-07", "time": "21:33:43", "dateTime": "2024-08-07T21:33:43Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-08-07T20:45:55Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.615686297416687, "url": "https://gamerant.com/fallout-london-find-bank-of-england-keys-location/", "title": "Where to Find the Bank of England Keys in Fallout London", "body": "Quick Links\n\nWhat Is The Bank Of England In Fallout London?\n\nThe Bank of England Key Location\n\nThe Bank Pindar Key Card Location\n\nBank of England Vault Key Card Location\n\nBank Manager Key Location\n\nFallout 4 has seen a ton of excitement recently due to the Fallout show produced with Amazon and then the release of the Fallout London mod, which is the largest mod for the game to date. The mod takes players around the streets of London and lets them see the historic city in Fallout fashion.\n\nWhile roaming the streets of London, players will be asked to take on the Bank of England during the Heavenslayer quest, which is a pretty important quest in the game. During the Wayfarer's visit, they will need to find several different sets of keys. Here's how to find the keys to the Bank of England.\n\nRelated\n\nFallout London: Crystalline Photon Agitator Location\n\nDuring the quest \"Swan and Mitre\" in Fallout London, you'll need to find a missing component for Bullettooth Anthony's latest project.\n\nWhat Is The Bank Of England In Fallout London?\n\nThe Bank of England is the mod's version of the real-life location of the Bank of England. This location will be visited during the Heavenslayer quest, and is basically a giant maze for players to figure out how to navigate. During the quest, players will meet Kiera, who is one of the more popular companions in the mod. Considering this is where Kiera is, most players will want to head here for her if nothing else. However, upon entering the Bank of England, players will come across a door that is locked and says it requires the \"Bank of England Key\" to unlock. While the Bank of England Key is needed to unlock the door, players will need to find three more keys to completely clear the Bank of England. Since this is the case, here's a breakdown of each of these key locations.\n\nPlayers will need to find the following keys in order to truly explore the bank and get everything needed: the Bank of England Key, the Bank Manager's Key, the Pindar Key Card, and the Bank Vault Key Card.\n\nRelated\n\nAll Settlements & Their Locations in Fallout London\n\nFallout London has 6 Settlements (7 if you count a home). Here's how to find them all.\n\nThe Bank of England Key Location\n\nUpon entering the Bank of England, turn left and go until finding the staircase with a door below it. Inside the door, players will find a hallway that they can travel down. At the end of the hallway, players can turn right and will find another hallway. At the end of this hallway, players will find a room with a large amount of smoke and a dead body hanging from the ceiling. There is also a door that will lead to the stairs to the second floor of the bank, go up the stairs. Finally, the keys will be hanging at the end of the hallway at the top of the stairs.\n\nRelated\n\nFallout London: All Factions (& How To Join Them)\n\nFallout London offers players different Factions. Here's how to join them all.\n\nThe Bank Pindar Key Card Location\n\nOnce players have found the Bank of England Key, they can head through the door in front of them to reach the main entrance of the bank. From there, go straight and look for a gray room with stairs in it, which players can take to the third floor. On the third floor, players will find an office at the end of the hallway that has two chairs and a desk in it. The Bank Pindar Key Card is on the desk by the broken computer.\n\nRelated\n\nAll Beer Coaster Locations in Fallout London\n\nFallout London has 30 Beer Coasters that replace Bobbleheads. Here's where to find them all.\n\nBank of England Vault Key Card Location\n\nFrom the entrance of the bank, turn left and head down the hallway until finding a door with a staircase behind it that leads down. Take the stairs all the way down until entering into the bunker below the vault. Once down there, players will find a bedroom with a table in it, which is where the Bank Vault Key Card is located.\n\nRelated\n\nHow to Play Fallout London With an Existing Character\n\nWhile Fallout London wasn't made for players to use their Fallout 4 characters, they are able to do so and here's how.\n\nBank Manager Key Location\n\nWith the other three keys in hand, players can now go through the locked double doors and can unlock the door that is chained within the room. Behind this door is the garden of the bank, and the bank's manager can be found within one of the Preservation Pods. His key will be located on the ground beside him, allowing players to access the rest of the bank (and even free Kiera).\n\nFallout 4\n\nSystems\n\nPlatform(s) PC , PS4 , PS5 , Xbox One , Xbox Series The arc in question is a Fallout New Vegas-style Wild Card option, and it's set to be deployed properly in a future update.\n\nYep, stop thinking about crashes for a minute, there's a British equivalent of Yes Man's Strip-conquering adventure with The Courier just chilling behind the scenes, after Team FOLON was forced to abandon including it in the initial release.\n\nSpeaking to VG247 for an interview which you'll be able to read more of here over the next little bit and also featured chat about the modders' current plans to rectify its pesky release bugs, Fallout: London project manager Dean 'Prilladog' Carter revealed some details about this questline, and why the team wasn't able to include it in the initial release.\n\n\"That was going to be in on launch, but if you can remember back to when we did our first announcement where we said we were not going to be releasing at the end of 2023, the guy that was in charge of doing the Wild Card quest line, which is what you're referring to, he wasn't able to do it [any longer] because he was basically forcibly conscripted due to the [Russo-Ukrainian] war,\" the modder explained, \"So, as you can imagine, working on a Fallout mod was not his top priority.\n\n\"All the lines have been recorded, all the systems [have been made]. That's why people might have noticed when they're walking around, there are certain buildings or levels of the building you can't get into. It's because it was designed to be there for release, but something like that is completely out of anyone's control, I don't care if you're a big company or not. That was so out of left field and you're just like 'oh'.\n\n\"So, that will be coming in a future patch, and then you'll be probably walking around like, 'Ah, that's why that door was locked and there's a whole building behind it.' We had to basically seal everything off very quickly, but that will be coming in a future patch.\"\n\nRegarding the war, which has also caused issues for other games such as Stalker 2, Carter added: \"Quite a lot of our scripting team were around those areas, and yeah, it impacted. So that's why I had to find myself learning scripting very quickly, it's why our head writer is also now the head writer/head scripter. We had to reshuffle and a lot of us had to learn very, very quickly.\n\n\"That's why, like, I'm not even gonna lie when I say that some of the quests, maybe the implementation side behind the backend is not as good as it could be. We couldn't help what happened in that situation. You know, it was going on as it could, we had everything all planned and sorted and all the quests that he had done were all bulletproof and then suddenly boom, [that person] has to go, like that was not an option, they then had to leave.\"\n\nAre you looking forward to seeing what this Wild Card quest for Fallout: London looks like when it arrives at some point down the line? Fallout New Vegas director Josh Sawyer believes that one of the RPG's world designers brilliantly demonstrated how to reward the player in this opening section of the game.\n\n\"Eric Fenstermaker was the designer of that area, and he ensured that every skill you could take would be rewarded within the ghost town gunfight and in the area,\" Sawyer says in the video below, around the 90-second mark. \"That was our way of telling the player 'Hey if you tagged this skill and you just started playing the game, we're here and we're paying attention to the character you made, and we're going to give you rewards for that.'\"\n\nFallout New Vegas' opening is generally highly regarded among the game's extensive community. In contrast to other games in the series like Fallout 3 or 4, you don't begin by emerging from an underground vault but instead begin as a courier, shot in the head and left for dead by Benny, the RPG's secondary antagonist (and portrayed by the late Matthew Perry).\n\nLater on in the video, shortly after the five-minute mark, Sawyer speaks a little more about 'skill checks' in Fallout New Vegas. \"The number of checks across all of your skills probably should be frontloaded. In the first couple of hours you really want to make the promise like 'hey, we are rewarding you for the things you invested in,'\" Sawyer says, again speaking to the Goodsprings section of New Vegas.\n\n\"As the game goes on, that density can drop off across the board, but as long as you keep rewarding the player for their choices over time enough, then they will feel like they're being rewarded, enough to make it worthwhile,\" the veteran RPG and Obsidian developer concludes.\n\nEarlier this month in June, Sawyer said players who didn't get along with Fallout New Vegas' very {"uri": "2024-08-443907608", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-08-04", "time": "22:19:54", "dateTime": "2024-08-04T22:19:54Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-08-04T22:00:11Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.5568627715110779, "url": "https://screenrant.com/fallout-4-how-to-get-companion-perks-affinity/", "title": "How To Get Companion Perks In Fallout 4", "body": "One Minor Fallout: London Quest Perfectly Shows Its Biggest Flaw\n\nQuick Links\n\nHow To Unlock Fallout 4 Companion Perks\n\nAll Fallout 4 Companion Perks\n\nIn a world as harsh as Fallout 4's post-apocalyptic wasteland, it's a good idea to have someone watching the Sole Survivor's back. Companions are a perfect way to do just that: helping out in combat and sometimes offering their opinions during quests. However, one of the best aspects of Fallout 4's companions is their perks, which are special bonuses that are unique to them.\n\nFallout 4 offers 16 companions who can travel with and aid the Sole Survivor during their mission to find Shaun. Getting companions in Fallout 4 is simple, but the method can vary between the different individuals on offer. Some will require completing a specific quest or joining their faction first, while others can quickly be hired for the right amount of caps. With each offering different skills and distinct outlooks on the world, it is well worth picking up as many companions as possible during any playthrough.\n\nRelated\n\n11 Must-Have Perks in Fallout 4\n\nThere are a total of 70 Perks in Fallout 4 and deciding which to pick can make all the difference for survival. 11 of these are crucial to take.\n\nHow To Unlock Fallout 4 Companion Perks\n\nLearning What Each Character Responds To Is Key\n\nClose\n\nTo get the individual companion perks in Fallout 4, the Sole Survivor will need to increase their affinity with each companion. The affinity system is designed so that the companions respond to the Sole Survivor based on their own personal likes and dislikes. The idea is that each companion will feel more realistic as they respond to actions or dialogue in keeping with their backgrounds and beliefs.\n\nAll companions will start at zero affinity with the Sole Survivor, which is neutral, and from there, their opinion can go either up or down. At key affinity values, dialogues will trigger, and in the case of positive affinity, this will further the relationship. Positive affinity can also lead to companion quests in some cases, which will be required to reach the next level of affinity for that particular companion.\n\nAffinity\n\nRelationship\n\nReaction\n\n1000+\n\nIdolize\n\nPerk unlocked.\n\n1000\n\nInfatuation\n\nNew dialogue triggered.\n\n750\n\nConfidant\n\nNew dialogue triggered.\n\n500\n\nAdmiration\n\nNew dialogue triggered.\n\n250\n\nFriend\n\nNew dialogue triggered.\n\n0\n\nNeutral\n\n-500\n\nDisdain\n\nNew dialogue triggered.\n\n-1000\n\nHatred\n\nCompanion will refuse to travel with Sole Survivor.\n\nWhen traveling with companions, a notice frequently appears to let the Sole Survivor know how a companion feels about something they have just said or done. There are only four reactions, but each will impact affinity either positively or negatively. \"X loved that\" will result in +35, while hate is -35, and likewise, \"X liked that\" is +15, while disliked is -15.\n\nIt is important to learn what each companion responds to and plan which quests to take them on or which actions to perform. For example, Paladin Danse will not like it if the Sole Survivor is pro-Synth or if they use Chems. However, Deacon would respond very positively to pro-Synth actions, and Hancock approves of Chem use. Most companions will hate it if they witness the Sole Survivor murder someone; however, Strong and Gage will have very positive reactions to the act.\n\nDogmeat and Ada do not have affinity scores and will stay with the Sole Survivor regardless of any actions taken. Ada has no companion perk, while Dogmeat's perk must be chosen when leveling up.\n\nAll Fallout 4 Companion Perks\n\nCompanion Perks Can Dictate Which Companion Focus On First\n\nClose\n\nSome perks are better suited to certain character builds than others, so it is best to prioritize those companions first. For example, Deacon's perk is great for a stealth build, while Piper's is best gained early to maximize XP gain. There are also perks that can only be gained after a companion's personal quest has been completed, such as with Cait, Danse, and MacCready.\n\nRelated\n\nFallout 4: Should You Side With Paladin Danse Or Elder Maxson\n\nBlind Betrayal comes near the end of Fallout 4's Brotherhood of Steel questline and forces the player to make some tough choices about Paladin Danse.\n\nCompanion\n\nInitial Harmonics: Resistance to energy weapons increased by 20.\n\nThere are 14 companion perks to unlock in Fallout 4, each providing a boost to a skill, damage, or damage resistance. For convenience, you can reach it by going southwest from Jalbert Brothers Disposal. But as we said earlier, this place is worth visiting at a certain time, namely after you start the Reunions quest. This way, players will gain access to the underground part of the location, which contains most of the loot.\n\nWhat to Expect From Fort Hagen in Fallout 4\n\nFirst of all, Fort Hagen in Fallout 4 has turrets that stand on the roof of the building. Therefore, even getting close to it isn't easy. In addition, there will be a lot of Synths waiting for you inside, so you should prepare well before you explore this location.\n\nAlso, it is worth noting that there are only two ways to get inside the building. The first method is the easiest, as you need to go to the garage on the side of the building. There, you will find a door that leads to the first floor of Fort Hagen in Fallout 4. For the second method, the Sole Survivor must climb the scaffolding on the northwest side.\n\nIf you come there with active Reunions, you can use the elevator. It will take you down to the basement, which will lead you to the Fort Hagen Command Center.
